                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, M, Msb, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="$aqu3a">شَقُقَ</orth>
                  </form>, (M, Msb,) <pb n="1576"/> inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَقٌّ</foreign>, (S, M, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He cut it</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">divided it</hi>] <hi rend="ital">lengthwise;</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">قد</foreign>;) [i. e.] <hi rend="ital">he clave it, split it, rived</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rifted it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">slit it; so as to separate it;</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">he clave, split, rived</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rifted, slit, rent, ripped, tore, broke,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">burst, it asunder;</hi>] or <hi rend="ital">without separating it;</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">he cracked, chapped, incided</hi> or <hi rend="ital">incised, gashed, slashed, furrowed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">trenched, it;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">clave, split,</hi> &amp;c., or <hi rend="ital">cut, it open;</hi>] syn. <foreign lang="ar">صَدَعَهُ</foreign>; (K;) or [more explicitly] <foreign lang="ar">الشَّقُّ</foreign> signifies <foreign lang="ar">الصَّدْعُ البَائِنُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the cleaving</hi> &amp;c. <hi rend="ital">that separates</hi>]; or <foreign lang="ar">غَيْرُ البَائِنِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">that which does not separate</hi>]; or <foreign lang="ar">الصَّدْعُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the cleaving,</hi> &amp;c.,] <hi rend="ital">in a general sense:</hi> (M:) and in like manner, [but with an intensive signification, or implying frequency or repetition of the action, or its application to several objects, generally meaning <hi rend="ital">he clave it,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">much,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in pieces,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in several places,</hi>]   
      <anchor/><foreign lang="ar"><ref cref="n22690-1" target="شقّقهُ" n="1" type="3" subtype="PO" lang="ar"/> </foreign>: (M, K:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">شقّق الحَطَبَ</foreign> (S, K) <foreign lang="ar">وَغَيْرَهُ</foreign> (S) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّهُ</foreign> [but properly meaning <hi rend="ital">He clave in pieces the firewood &amp;c.</hi>]. (K. [In the CK, <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ الحَطَبَ</foreign> is erroneously put for <foreign lang="ar">شقّق</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحطب</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ رَأْسَهُ</foreign> generally means <hi rend="ital">He clave his head,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">his pericranium:</hi> and sometimes, as in an instance in the K voce <foreign lang="ar">شَقَأَ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">he divided the hair of his head.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ العَصَا</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He split the staff</hi>] means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">he separated himself from the community;</hi> (S, K, TA;) and particularly, that of the Muslims: because the staff is not thus called but when it is whole, not when it is split: accord. to Lth, <foreign lang="ar">يَشُقُّ عَصَا المُسْلِمِينَ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22690-2" target="يُشَاقُّهُمْ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> signify alike: but they differ in meaning, as will be shown hereafter. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ عَصَا المُسْلِمِينَ</foreign>, K, TA,) said of a <foreign lang="ar">خَارِجِىّ</foreign> [i. e. heretic or schismatic], also means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He effected disunion and dissension in the body of the Muslims.</hi> (TA.) And one says also, <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ عَصَا الطَّاعَةِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He broke the compact of allegiance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">obedience; became a rebel</hi>]. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">لَا وَالَّذِى شَقَّ الرِّجَالَ لِلْخَيْلِ وَالجِبَالَ لِلسَّيْلِ</foreign> [app. meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">No, by Him who clave men for</hi> the riding upon <hi rend="ital">horses, and the mountains for</hi> the flowing of <hi rend="ital">the torrent,</hi>] is a saying mentioned by IAar, but not expl. by him. (M. [It is there added, <foreign lang="ar">وَعِنْدِى أَنَّهُ جَعَلَ الرِّجَالَ وَالجِبَالَ جُمْلَةً</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدَةً ثُمَّ خَرَقَهُمَا فَجَعَلَ الرِّجَالَ لِهٰذِهِ وَالجِبَالَ لِهٰذَا</foreign>: an expression of opinion which is, to me, by no means clear, though reconcilable with my rendering.])          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">المَالُ بَيْنَنَا شَقَّ الأَبْلَمَةِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الأُبْلُمَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The property is</hi> divided <hi rend="ital">between us as in the dividing of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ابلمة</foreign>; or <hi rend="ital">the cattle are</hi> divided &amp;c.;] means we are equal in respect of the property, or cattle: for the <foreign lang="ar">ابلمة</foreign> means the [kind of leaf called] <foreign lang="ar">خُوصَة</foreign>, which, when it is split lengthwise, splits in halves: (M:) or, accord. to Aboo-Ziyád, the <foreign lang="ar">ابلمة</foreign> is a herb, or leguminous plant, (<foreign lang="ar">بَقْلَةٌ</foreign>,) to which there come forth pods, like [those of] the bean; and when you split them lengthwise, they split in halves, equally, from the first part to the last thereof: <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ</foreign> is in the accus. case as an inf. n., <foreign lang="ar">مَشْقُوقٌ</foreign> being understood. (Har p. 639.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">شِقٌّ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="$aqu3a">شَقُقَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شُقُوقٌ</foreign>, (M,) said of the canine tooth of a camel, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">It</hi> [<hi rend="ital">clave the gum and</hi>] <hi rend="ital">came forth:</hi> (S, M, K, TA:) [said to be] a dial. var. of <foreign lang="ar">شَقَأَ</foreign>: (S:) and said of the canine tooth of a child, (M, TA,) in like manner, (TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">it made its first appearance:</hi> (M:) and said also of a plant, [as meaning <hi rend="ital">it came forth</hi>] <hi rend="ital">on the ground's first cleaving open from it.</hi> (M, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  Also, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="$aqu3a">شَقُقَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَقٌّ</foreign>, said of the dawn, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">It rose;</hi> as though it clave the place of its rising and came forth therefrom. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  Also, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="$aqu3a">شَقُقَ</orth>
                  </form>, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَقٌّ</foreign>, said of lightning, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">It</hi> [<hi rend="ital">clave the clouds, and</hi>] <hi rend="ital">extended high, into the midst of the sky, without going to the right and left:</hi> (K, TA:) so says A'Obeyd: (TA: [see <foreign lang="ar">شَقِيقٌ</foreign>:]) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22690-3" target="انشقّ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n22695"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22690-4" target="تشقّق" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n22693"/></foreign>, said of lightning, signify <foreign lang="ar">اِنْعَقَّ</foreign> [probably meaning the same; (see <foreign lang="ar">عَقِيقَةٌ</foreign>;) or, as expl. in the S and also in the O, in art. <foreign lang="ar">عق</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">it was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, in a state of commotion,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">تَضَرَّبَ</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">in the clouds</hi>]: (M, TA:) or

                  </form> [accord. to Golius, <hi rend="ital">A fissure;</hi> as from the KL; but not so expl. in my copy of that work.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense> ] <hi rend="ital">An intervening space</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tract between two elongated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">extended, tracts of sand,</hi> (S, M, * O, K, * [in the last of which <foreign lang="ar">الجَبَلَيْنِ</foreign> is erroneously put for <foreign lang="ar">الجَبْلَيْنِ</foreign>,]) thus expl. to AHn by an Arab of the desert, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">producing herbage:</hi> (S, M, O, K:) or <hi rend="ital">a rugged tract between two elongated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">extended, tracts of sand, producing good herbage;</hi> (M, TA;) so in the T, as expl. to its author by an Arab of the desert: (TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">شَقَائِقُ</foreign>, (T, S, O, K, TA,) expl. by some as meaning <hi rend="ital">sands</hi> themselves: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a great piece of sand:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a piece of sand between two pieces thereof.</hi> (Ham p. 282.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [In the A and TA voce <foreign lang="ar">قِطُّ</foreign>, it is used as meaning <hi rend="ital">A slice cut off</hi> of a melon &amp;c.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A rain,</hi> (M,) or <hi rend="ital">a violent rain, consisting of large drops,</hi> (K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">wide in extent:</hi> so called because the clouds cleave asunder from it: (M, K, TA:) pl. as above. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  The pl., <foreign lang="ar">شَقَائِقُ</foreign>, is expl. by Az as signifying <hi rend="ital">Clouds that have cloven asunder with copious rains.</hi> (O, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَقِيقَةُ بَرْقٍِ</foreign>, (O, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">عَقِيقَتُهُ</foreign>, both as expl. by Aboo-Sa'eed, (O,) <hi rend="ital">A flash of lightning that has spread</hi> (O, K) <hi rend="ital">in the horizon,</hi> (O,) or <hi rend="ital">from the horizon:</hi> (K: [but see <foreign lang="ar">شَقِيقُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">البَرْقِ</foreign>:]) or <foreign lang="ar">شَقِيقَةٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">a flash of lightning that has spread in the breadth of the clouds, and filled the sky:</hi> pl. as above. (Ham p. 557.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A headache,</hi> (JK, T, TA,) or <hi rend="ital">a pain,</hi> (S, O, K,) or <hi rend="ital">a certain disease,</hi> (M,) <hi rend="ital">in the half of the head,</hi> (JK, T, S, M, O, K,) [i. e. <hi rend="ital">hemicrania,</hi>] and <hi rend="ital">of the face:</hi> (JK, T, S, O, K:) or, accord. to IAth, <hi rend="ital">a sort of headache in the fore part of the head and towards the sides thereof.</hi> (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="4">-A4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَقَائِقُ النُّعْمَانِ</foreign>, used alike as sing. and pl., (S, O, K,) having no proper sing., (Msb,) or its sing. is <foreign lang="ar">شَقِيقَةٌ</foreign>; (M, O, Msb;) [The <hi rend="ital">red,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">blood-coloured, anemone;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a certain plant;</hi> (M;) <hi rend="ital">a certain red flower;</hi> (Lth, O;) <hi rend="ital">well known;</hi> (S, K;) the <foreign lang="ar">شَقِر</foreign>; (Msb;) or, as AHn says, on the authority of AA and Aboo-Nasr and others, it is the <foreign lang="ar">شَقِرَة</foreign> [n. un. of <foreign lang="ar">شَقِرٌ</foreign>]; and the sing. of <foreign lang="ar">شقائق</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">شَقِيقَةٌ</foreign>: (O, TA:) it is called <foreign lang="ar">شقائق النعمان</foreign> because of its redness, as being likened to the <foreign lang="ar">شَقِيقَة</foreign> of lightning: (M, K:) or from <foreign lang="ar">النُّعْمَان</foreign> as meaning “ blood, ” as resembling blood in colour; (Msb, TA;) so that it signifies “ pieces of blood: ” (TA:) or in relation to En-Noamán Ibn-El-Mundhir, because he prohibited to the public a piece of land in which it abounded: (S, K, TA:) or because he alighted upon <foreign lang="ar">شَقَائِق</foreign> of sand that had produced red <foreign lang="ar">شَقِر</foreign>, and he deemed them beautiful, and commanded that they should be prohibited to the public; (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  To this is likened the tongue of the chaste, or eloquent, and able speaker; himself being likened to the braying stallion-camel: (O:) and hence they say of an orator, or a preacher, that he is <foreign lang="ar">ذُو شِقْشِقَةٍ</foreign>: (S:) one says likewise of an orator, or a preacher, that is loud in voice and skilful in speech, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ أَهْرَتُ الشِقْشِقَةِ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He is wide,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ample, in respect of the</hi>
